Second Proof: Killing a Believer Deliberately
Razi presents the second Mu'tazilite proof using verse 4:93, with a brief objection and response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second Mu'tazilite proof that the intentional killer of a believer deserves eternal Hell, based on Quranic verses and the principle of general wording.

Core Idea
A Quranic threat applies generally, not just to its specific occasion.

Razi now presents another proof from the Mu'tazila: a direct Quranic verse threatening eternal Hell for anyone who intentionally kills a believer. The argument relies on two moves: first, that such a threat must be carried out (as supported by another verse), and second, that the verse's general wording covers all believers, not just the original context. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and the refutation of a potential objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the proof is structured: a main verse, a supporting verse, an objection, and a response.
The Arabic is concise. Pause after each sentence.
2
Understand the proof's logic
Identify the two Quranic verses and how they connect. The first gives the punishment; the second implies it must be applied.
The Mu'tazila assume that Allah's threat is true and must be fulfilled.
3
Examine the objection and response
The objection is that the verse was revealed about disbelievers. The response uses the principle of 'general wording, not specific cause.'
This principle is crucial in Islamic legal theory (usul al-fiqh).
4
Reflect on the principle
Consider why the Mu'tazila insist on general application. How does this strengthen their case for eternal punishment?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِنًا مُّتَعَمِّدًا فَجَزَاؤُهُ جَهَنَّمُ خَالِدًا فِيهَا﴾ [النساء : ٩٣] وإذا ثبت أن جزاءه ذلك وجب أن يصل إليه، لقوله تعالى: ﴿مَن يَعْمَلْ سُوءًا يُجْزَ بِهِ﴾ [النساء : ١٢٣] لا يقال : نزلت في بعض الكفار ؛ لأنا نقول : العبرة بعموم اللفظ لا بخصوص السبب.
The second proof: His saying, exalted: {And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding eternally therein} [al-Nisa: 93]. And if it is established that his recompense is that, then it must befall him, because of His saying, exalted: {Whoever does evil will be recompensed for it} [al-Nisa: 123]. It cannot be said: It was revealed concerning some disbelievers; for we say: The lesson is by the generality of the wording, not by the specificity of the cause.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This is a proof citation with a brief objection and answer. The Mu'tazila cite verse 4:93 that whoever intentionally kills a believer will have Hell as his recompense and remain there eternally. They argue that this punishment must actually occur, supported by the general principle in verse 4:123 that whoever does evil will be repaid for it. The potential objection (that the verse was revealed about specific disbelievers) is rejected on the principle that legal rulings follow the general wording of the text, not the particular occasion of revelation. Thus the verse applies to any believer who commits intentional murder.

Key Terms
الجزاء
عموم اللفظ
خصوص السبب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse (4:93) only applies to the specific disbelievers for whom it was revealed.
Correction: The Mu'tazila argue that the general wording of the verse ('whoever kills a believer intentionally') applies to all such cases, not just the original context, based on the principle 'al-ibrah bi-umum al-lafz la bi-khusus al-sabab'.

Checkpoint
What principle do the Mu'tazila use to reject the claim that the verse was revealed about disbelievers?
A) The verse is clear in its wording.
B) The generality of the wording is considered, not the particular cause.
C) The verse is universally applicable.
D) The prophet's actions are instructive.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila argue that Quran 4:93, supported by 4:123, proves that anyone who intentionally kills a believer will be eternally punished in Hell, and this applies to all cases because the wording is general.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read Quran 4:93, do you automatically assume it applies to others but not to you because you consider yourself a believer? What does that assumption say about your view of God's justice? Will you now accept that the verse applies to you personally if you ever commit such a sin?
?
The Mu'tazila refused to let the occasion of revelation water down the verse's threat. Are there verses in the Quran that you have been making exceptions for in your own life? If so, what is one specific verse you need to stop rationalizing? Take a moment to write down how you will obey it.
?
If you were to stand before God having committed a major sin, would you trust in His mercy alone or would you also believe that His justice demands punishment? How does this lesson challenge your reliance on easy forgiveness? Make a firm commitment to change one habit that you have been treating as a 'small' sin.

Third Proof: The Verse of Fleeing from Battle
Razi cites Quran 8:16 as the third Mu'tazilite proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite argument based on Quran 8:16 that fleeing from battle incurs eternal punishment, and how this proof fits into their doctrine.

Core Idea
The threat of Hell for fleeing battle is used to prove eternal punishment for grave sinners.

The Mu'tazila cite Quran 8:16 as evidence that believers who commit the grave sin of fleeing from battle will be eternally punished. This proof relies on the apparent unconditional threat of Hell, despite the verse's exceptions. Let's examine the verse and the reasoning behind this argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse in context
Start by reading the Arabic verse and its translation. Notice the structure: a command (do not turn back), a threat (incurred wrath and Hell), and exceptions (maneuvering or joining a company).
The verse is from Surah al-Anfal, revealed in the context of the Battle of Badr.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite reasoning
The Mu'tazila take the unconditional threat ('whoever turns back... his abode is Hell') as a general ruling. They argue that this threat applies to any believer who flees, implying eternal punishment for grave sinners.
They ignore the exceptions or interpret them narrowly.
3
Consider the counterargument
Reflect on the exceptions in the verse: maneuvering for battle or joining a company. The Ash'ari response might note that the threat is conditional on not being within these exceptions, or that the verse is about a specific battle, not a general rule.
This shows how the same verse can be used differently by different schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : قوله تعالى: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذَا لَقِيتُمُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا زَحْفًا فَلَا تُوَلُّوهُمُ الْأَدْبَارَ وَمَن يُوَلِّهِمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ دُبُرَهُ إِلَّا مُتَحَرِّفًا لِقِتَالٍ أَوْ مُتَحَيِّزًا إِلَى فِئَةٍ فَقَدْ بَاءَ بِغَضَبٍ مِنَ اللَّهِ وَمَأْوَاهُ جَهَنَّمُ وَبِئْسَ الْمَصِيرُ﴾ [الأنفال: ١٦]
The third proof: His saying, exalted: {O you who have believed, when you meet those who disbelieve in battle, do not turn your backs to them. And whoever turns his back to them on that day – unless maneuvering for battle or intending to join a company – has indeed incurred wrath from God, and his abode is Hell, and wretched is the destination} [al-Anfal: 16].
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This is a straightforward citation of a proof. The Mu'tazila use the verse that those who flee from battle (without valid excuse) incur God's wrath and their abode is Hell. They take this as evidence that believers who commit this sin will be eternally punished, assuming the threat is general.

Key Terms
الغضب
مأوى
جهنم
الفرار من الزحف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse unconditionally threatens all who flee from battle with Hell, with no exceptions.
Correction: The verse actually includes two exceptions: maneuvering for battle or intending to join a company. These exceptions show the threat is not absolute.

Checkpoint
What act does the verse in this lesson threaten with God's wrath and Hell?
A) Killing a believer.
B) Fleeing from battle.
C) Disobeying limits.
D) Committing murder.

Key Takeaway
The third Mu'tazilite proof uses Quran 8:16 to argue that believers who flee battle earn eternal damnation, supporting their doctrine of eternal punishment for grave sinners.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that turning your back in battle incurs God's wrath and Hell. But what about the battles you face daily against your own desires and temptations? Have you turned your back on a command of Allah because it was difficult? What specific step will you take today to stand firm in obedience, knowing that every retreat from duty is a form of fleeing?
?
The verse allows exceptions for tactical maneuvers. Are there times when you have used a 'valid exception' to justify disobedience when your real motive was fear or laziness? Ask Allah to give you sincerity in following His commands without seeking loopholes.
?
The Mu'tazilites see this verse as proof of eternal punishment for grave sins. Regardless of your theological position, does the warning of Hellfire in this verse truly move you? When was the last time you wept out of fear of Allah's wrath? What will you change in your life so that this fear becomes a driving force for repentance?

Five Mu'tazilite Proof Texts from the Quran
Razi lists five additional Mu'tazilite proofs from Quranic verses, with the eighth incomplete.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand five Quranic verses that the Mu'tazilites used as proof texts for their doctrine that believing wrongdoers deserve punishment.

Core Idea
Mu'tazilites used Quranic threats to argue that any wrongdoer, including believers, deserves punishment.

Imam al-Razi continues his enumeration of Mu'tazilite arguments based on Quranic verses that promise punishment for evil deeds. These verses are presented as proof that even believers who commit sins will face consequences. In this lesson, we examine five such proof texts, though the final one is incomplete.

Guided Path
1
Read each proof verse carefully
Read the Arabic text and translation for each of the five proofs. Notice how the Mu'tazilites interpret these general threats as applying to all wrongdoers, including believers.
2
Identify the common theme
Observe that each verse uses strong language of punishment (fire, penalty, failure). The Mu'tazilites argue that if these threats apply universally, they must include sinful believers.
3
Reflect on the eighth proof's incompleteness
The eighth proof is cut off. Consider how the Mu'tazilites might have completed this argument.
The full verse is from al-Furqan 25:68-69.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ خَيْرًا يَرَهُ وَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ شَرًّا يَرَهُ﴾ [الزلزلة: ٧-٨] . الحجة الخامسة: قوله تعالى : ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا تَأْكُلُوا أَمْوَالَكُمْ بَيْنَكُمْ بِالْبَاطِلِ﴾ [النساء: ٢٩] إلى قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يَفْعَلْ ذَلِكَ عُدْوَانًا وَظُلْمًا فَسَوْفَ نُصْلِيهِ نَارًا﴾ [النساء: ٣٠] . الحجة السادسة: قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّهُ مَن يَأْتِ رَبَّهُ مُجْرِمًا فَإِنَّ لَهُ جَهَنَّمَ لَا يَمُوتُ فِيهَا وَلَا يَحْيَى﴾ [طه: ٧٤] . الحجة السابعة : قوله تعالى : ﴿وَقَدْ خَابَ مَنْ حَمَلَ ظُلْمًا﴾ [طه: ١١١] ولا شك أن هذا الوعيد يتناول الظالم سواء كان كافرًا أو مؤمنًا. الحجة الثامنة : أنه تعالى قال بعد تعديد المعاصي : ﴿ وَمَن يَفْعَلْ ذَلِكَ يَلْقَ أَثَامًا﴾
The fourth proof: His saying, exalted: {So whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it, and whoever does an atom's weight of evil will see it} [al-Zalzalah: 7-8]. The fifth proof: His saying, exalted: {O you who have believed, do not consume your wealth among yourselves unjustly} [al-Nisa: 29] up to His saying, exalted: {And whoever does that in aggression and injustice, We will roast him in a fire} [al-Nisa: 30]. The sixth proof: His saying, exalted: {Indeed, whoever comes to his Lord as a criminal, then indeed for him is Hell; he will neither die therein nor live} [Taha: 74]. The seventh proof: His saying, exalted: {And indeed he fails who carries injustice} [Taha: 111]. And there is no doubt that this threat encompasses the wrongdoer, whether he is a disbeliever or a believer. The eighth proof: That He, exalted, said after enumerating sins: {And whoever does that will meet [the penalty of] sin}
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage lists several more Mu'tazilite proofs in quick succession. The fourth uses the verse from al-Zalzalah that everyone will see the consequences of their good or evil deeds, implying punishment for evil. The fifth combines two parts of a verse from al-Nisa' to threaten those who consume wealth unjustly with being roasted in fire. The sixth cites Taha 74 that criminals will be cast into Hell where they neither die nor live (eternal torment). The seventh cites Taha 111 that whoever carries injustice will fail, explicitly stating that this applies to both believers and disbelievers, thus arguing that a believing wrongdoer is threatened. The eighth proof begins but is cut off; it refers to a verse after enumerating sins, likely from al-Furqan (25:68-69), threatening with penalty.

The Boundary Argument: Threat Applies to Transgressors of Inheritance
Razi refutes an objection by specifying inheritance boundaries as the referent of the threat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses contextual interpretation to restrict the application of a threat verse to inheritance boundaries, refuting the claim that it applies only to disbelievers.

Core Idea
The threat of transgression refers to specific inheritance rules, not all boundaries.

In this passage, Imam Razi addresses a common objection: how can anyone truly 'transgress all boundaries'? He shows that the verse's context—the preceding inheritance verses—limits the threat to those who violate the specific inheritance rules laid out by Allah. This demonstrates the importance of understanding Quranic context and pronoun reference.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Razi presents an objection: either transgressing all boundaries is impossible or only possible for a disbeliever. Read the passage to see this.
The objector uses logical alternatives to challenge the verse's applicability.
2
Identify Razi's refutation
Notice how Razi responds by specifying that 'boundaries' refers to the inheritance rules mentioned earlier in the Quranic passage.
3
Trace the pronoun reference
Razi points out that the phrase 'those boundaries' in Surah al-Nisa refers back to the inheritance boundaries in Surah al-Baqara. This is a key linguistic argument.
The Arabic pronoun 'tilka' (those) indicates a specific antecedent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحدود لا يصدق إلا عند تعدي جميع الحدود، وهو إما أن لا يكون ممكنا أو يكون ممكنا لكنه لا يثبت إلا في حق الكافر، أما أنه غير ممكن فلأن من تعدى بالمجوسية ذلك أن يتعدى باليهودية ومن تعدى بالفعل لا يمكنه في تلك الحالة أن يتعدى بالترك. وأيضًا: فإن كان ذلك ممكنا إلا أنه لا يتحقق إلا في حق الكافر، فكانت الآية مختصة بالكافر. قلنا : إنه تعالى شرح حدود الميراث في مقدمة هذه الآية، ثم قال: &#x7D9;تِلْكَ حُدُودُ اللَّهِ&#x7D9; [البقرة : ١٨٧] فانصرف هذا الحد إلى الحدود المذكورة فيما تقدم، وهي حدود الميراث، ثم قال: &#x7D9;وَمَن يَعْصِ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ وَيَتَعَدَّ حُدُودَهُ&#x7D9; [النساء : ١٤] فقوله: ويعد حُدُودَهُ لا يبعد أن يكون منصرفًا إلى الحدود المذكورة فيما قبل ذلك، فثبت أن هذا الوعيد مختص بمن تعدى الحدود المذكورة في الميراث.
The boundaries are not believed except when one transgresses all the boundaries. This is either impossible, or possible but only established in the case of the disbeliever. As for its being impossible, because whoever transgressed by Magianism, then he would transgress by Judaism, and whoever has already transgressed by action cannot in that state transgress by abandoning. Also: if that were possible, yet it only occurs in the case of the disbeliever, so the verse would be specific to the disbeliever. We say: He, exalted, explained the boundaries of inheritance in the preamble of this verse, then said: &quot;These are the boundaries of Allah&quot; (Surah al-Baqarah 2:187), so this boundary refers to the boundaries mentioned earlier, which are the boundaries of inheritance. Then He said: &quot;And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger and transgresses His boundaries&quot; (Surah al-Nisa 4:14). So His saying &quot;and transgresses His boundaries&quot; is not far from referring to the boundaries mentioned before that. Hence it is established that this threat is specific to whoever transgresses the boundaries mentioned regarding inheritance.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection and an argument establishing the context of a specific threat. The objector claims that the verse threatening those who transgress Allah's boundaries (hudud) cannot apply to anyone, because either one transgresses all boundaries (impossible) or only the disbeliever does so. Razi counters by identifying the referent of 'boundaries' in the verse: the preceding inheritance verses (Surah al-Baqara 2:187). Thus, the threat is specific to those who transgress the inheritance rules, not all boundaries. Razi shows that the phrase 'those boundaries' in Surah al-Nisa 4:14 refers back to the same inheritance boundaries, so the threat is limited to that context. The argument hinges on the principle that a pronoun can refer to a nearby antecedent.

الوعيد
الميراث
الآية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The threat of transgression applies to anyone who disobeys any of Allah's commands.
Correction: Razi argues that the context shows the threat is specifically about violating inheritance rules, not all commands.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's argument, to which boundaries does the threat of transgression specifically refer?
A) All divine boundaries in general
B) The boundaries of inheritance mentioned before the verse
C) Boundaries of jihad and warfare
D) Boundaries of prayer and fasting

Key Takeaway
Razi shows that the threat of transgression is limited to those who violate the specific inheritance boundaries, not all divine limits.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Are there areas in your life—like financial transactions or family rights—where you selectively apply Allah's commands, treating some as binding and others as optional? What would it take for you to honor His limits even when they seem inconvenient?
?
Razi's argument rests on the principle that even a pronoun in the Quran carries precise meaning. Do you treat Allah's words with that level of care in your own understanding? Where might you be neglecting the details of His revelation?

The Principle of General Wording in the Second Proof
Razi's second proof with its objection and answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the principle of 'umum al-lafz' (general wording) to argue that the threat of eternal Hell for killing a believer applies even if the killer is a believer.

Core Idea
Words matter, not specific causes—the verse speaks generally.

Razi begins his second proof with a clear Quranic threat: anyone who kills a believer intentionally will have Hell as recompense. He then defends its generality against a potential objection, establishing a key hermeneutical principle for the entire series of proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the second proof passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice how Razi cites the verse and then immediately applies it.
Pay attention to the objection and response.
2
Identify the hermeneutical principle
See how Razi counters the claim that the verse was revealed about a specific disbeliever by invoking 'al-ibrah bi umum al-lafz la bi khusus al-sabab'.
This principle is crucial for all subsequent proofs.
3
Connect to the broader debate
Understand why this matters: if the threat applies to any intentional killer, then a believing killer is not exempt from eternal punishment.
This refutes the Murji'ah claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِنَا مُّتَعَمِّدًا فَجَزَاؤُهُ جَهَنَّمُ خَالِدًا فِيهَا﴾ [النساء : ۹۳] وإذا ثبت أن جزاءه ذلك وجب أن يصل إليه، لقوله تعالى: ﴿مَن يَعْمَلْ سُوءًا يُجْزَ بِهِ﴾ [النساء : ۱۲۳] لا يقال : نزلت في بعض الكفار ؛ لأنا نقول : العبرة بعموم اللفظ لا بخصوص السبب. الحجة الثالثة : قوله تعالى: ﴿يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذا لَقِيتُمُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا زَحْفًا ... وَمَن يُوَلِّهِمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ دُبُرَهُ إِلَّا مُتَحَرِّفًا لِقِتَالٍ أَوْ مُتَحَيِّزًا إِلَى فِئَةٍ فَقَدْ بَاءَ بِغَضَبٍ مِنَ اللهِ وَمَأْوَاهُ جَهَنَّمُ وَبِئْسَ الْمَصِيرُ﴾ [الأنفال : ١٦] الحجة الرابعة : قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ خَيْرًا يَرَهُ وَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ شَرًّا يَرَهُ﴾ [الزلزلة : ۷ - ۸] . الحجة الخامسة: قوله تعالى: ﴿يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا تَأْكُلُوا أَمْوَالَكُمْ بَيْنَكُم بِالْبَاطِلِ﴾ [النساء : ۲۹] إلى قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يَفْعَلْ ذَلِكَ عُدْوَانًا وَظُلْمًا فَسَوْفَ نُصْلِيهِ نَارًا﴾ [النساء : ٣٠] . الحجة السادسة: قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّهُ مَن يَأْتِ رَبَّهُ مُجْرِمًا فَإِنَّ لَهُ جَهَنَّمَ لَا يَمُوتُ فِيهَا وَلَا يَحْيَا﴾ [طه: ٧٤]. الحجة السابعة : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَقَدْ خَابَ مَنْ حَمَلَ ظُلْمًا﴾ [طه: ۱۱۱] ولا شك أن هذا الوعيد يتناول الظالم سواء كان كافرًا أو مؤمنًا. الحجة الثامنة : أنه تعالى قال بعد تعديد المعاصي : ﴿وَمَن يَفْعَلْ ذَلِكَ يَلْقَ أَثَامًا يُضَاعَفْ لَهُ الْعَذَابُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ وَيَخْلُدْ فِيهِ مُهَانًا﴾ [الفرقان: ٦٨ - ٦٩] . الحجة التاسعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن جَاءَ بِالْحَسَنَةِ فَلَهُ خَيْرٌ مِنْهَا وَهُم مِّن فَزَعٍ يَوْمَئِذٍ آمِنُونَ وَمَن جَاءَ بِالسَّيِّئَةِ فَكُبَّتْ وُجُوهُهُمْ فِي النَّارِ هَلْ تُجْزَوْنَ إِلَّا مَا كُنتُمْ تَعْمَلُونَ﴾ [النمل: ۸۹ - ۹۰] فلما دل النصف الأول من هذه الآية على أن الوعد حاصل على الطاعات دل النصف الثاني على أن الوعيد حاصل على جميع المعاصي. الحجة العاشرة : قوله تعالى : ﴿فَأَمَّا مَن طَغَى وَآثَرَ الْحَيَاةَ الدُّنْيَا فَإِنَّ الْجَحِيمَ هِيَ الْمَأْوَى﴾ [النازعات : ٣٧ - ٣٩]. الحجة الحادية عشرة : أنه تعالى حكى قول المرجئة، فقال : ﴿وَقَالُوا لَن تَمَسَّنَا النَّارُ إِلَّا أَيَّامًا مَّعْدُودَةً﴾ [البَقَرَة : ۸۰] ثم إنه تعالى كذبهم في هذه المقالة بقوله : ﴿قُلْ أَخَذْتُمْ عِندَ اللهِ عَهْدًا فَلَنْ يُخْلِفَ اللهُ عَهْدَهُ أَمْ تَقُولُونَ عَلَى اللهِ مَا لَا تَعْلَمُونَ﴾ [البقرة : ٨٠] ثم ذكر المذهب الصحيح فقال : ﴿بَلَى مَن كَسَبَ سَيِّئَةً وَأَحَاطَتْ بِهِ خَطِيئَتُهُ فَأُولَئِكَ أَصْحَابُ النَّارِ هُمْ فِيهَا خَالِدُونَ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ۸۱].
The second proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding therein&quot; (Surah al-Nisa 4:93). And when it is established that his recompense is that, it must reach him, due to His saying, Exalted: &quot;Whoever does evil will be requited for it&quot; (Surah al-Nisa 4:123). It cannot be said: it was revealed concerning some disbelievers; because we say: consideration is given to the generality of the wording, not to the specificity of the cause. The third proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;O you who believe, when you meet those who disbelieve in battle... and whoever turns his back to them on that day, unless maneuvering for battle or joining a company, has indeed incurred the wrath of Allah, and his abode is Hell, and evil is the destination&quot; (Surah al-Anfal 8:16). The fourth proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;So whoever does an atom&#39;s weight of good will see it, and whoever does an atom&#39;s weight of evil will see it&quot; (Surah al-Zalzala 99:7-8). The fifth proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;O you who believe, do not consume your wealth among yourselves unjustly... and whoever does that in transgression and injustice, We will burn him in a fire&quot; (Surah al-Nisa 4:29-30). The sixth proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;Indeed, whoever comes to his Lord as a criminal, then for him is Hell; he will neither die therein nor live&quot; (Surah Ta-Ha 20:74). The seventh proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;And indeed he fails who carries injustice&quot; (Surah Ta-Ha 20:111). There is no doubt that this threat encompasses the oppressor, whether he is a disbeliever or a believer. The eighth proof: That He, Exalted, after enumerating sins, said: &quot;And whoever does that will meet a penalty; the punishment will be doubled for him on the Day of Resurrection, and he will abide therein humiliated&quot; (Surah al-Furqan 25:68-69). The ninth proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;And whoever comes with a good deed, for him is better than it, and they from the terror of that Day are secure. And whoever comes with an evil deed, their faces are thrust into the fire: &#39;Are you recompensed except for what you used to do?&#39;&quot; (Surah al-Naml 27:89-90). Since the first half of this verse indicates that the promise of reward is for acts of obedience, the second half indicates that the threat of punishment is for all acts of disobedience. The tenth proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;As for he who transgressed and preferred the life of this world, then indeed Hellfire is the refuge&quot; (Surah al-Nazi&#39;at 79:37-39). The eleventh proof: That He, Exalted, related the saying of the Murji&#39;ah: &quot;And they say, &#39;The fire will not touch us except for a limited number of days&#39;&quot; (Surah al-Baqara 2:80). Then He, Exalted, declared them false in this statement by His saying: &quot;Say, &#39;Have you taken a covenant with Allah? Then Allah will not break His covenant, or do you say about Allah what you do not know?&#39;&quot; (Surah al-Baqara 2:80). Then He mentioned the correct doctrine, saying: &quot;Yes, whoever earns evil and his sin surrounds him, those are the companions of the fire; they will abide therein eternally&quot; (Surah al-Baqara 2:81).
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage presents ten consecutive Quranic proofs (the second through the eleventh) supporting the position that divine threats of punishment encompass all sinners, including believers who commit major sins, contrary to the Murji&#39;ah view that only disbelievers are subject to eternal punishment. Each proof is a verse that imposes punishment in absolute or general terms. The second proof (4:93) threatens anyone who kills a believer intentionally with eternal Hell; Razi argues this applies even to a believer who kills another believer, and the principle of general wording (umum al-lafz) overrides any claim of specific cause. The third proof (8:16) threatens those who flee from battle with divine wrath and Hell. The fourth (99:7-8) promises reward and punishment for every atom&#39;s weight of good and evil, without restricting to disbelievers. The fifth (4:29-30) threatens fire for those who consume wealth unjustly. The sixth (20:74) states that every criminal who comes to his Lord will have Hell. The seventh (20:111) declares that anyone who bears injustice fails; Razi notes this includes both believer and disbeliever oppressors. The eighth (25:68-69) lists major sins and threatens doubled punishment and eternal abasement. The ninth (27:89-90) contrasts the security of those who bring good deeds with the casting into fire of those who bring evil deeds. The tenth (79:37-39) threatens Hell for those who transgress and prefer worldly life. The eleventh (2:80-81) directly refutes the Murji&#39;ah claim of limited punishment, asserting that those whose sin encompasses them are eternal inhabitants of the fire. Razi&#39;s method is to cite clear Quranic texts that either explicitly mention eternity for certain sins or use conditional particles like 'man' (whoever) and 'ma' (whatever) to indicate generality. The underlying principle is that these verses do not differentiate between believers and disbelievers in their threat, so they apply to all who commit the described sins.

Key Terms
الوعيد
العبرة بعموم اللفظ
المرجئة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Quranic threats like 4:93 only apply to disbelievers, not to believers who commit the same sin.
Correction: Razi shows that the generality of the wording ('whoever') includes all, and the specific historical cause does not limit its application.

Checkpoint
What principle does Razi use to respond to the objection that the verse was revealed about a disbeliever?
A) The verse is abrogated
B) Consideration is given to the generality of the wording, not the specificity of the cause
C) The verse applies only to the first addressees
D) The threat is metaphorical

Key Takeaway
Razi's second proof establishes that Quranic threats are general unless evidence restricts them, using the principle that 'consideration is given to the generality of the wording'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verse 4:93, do you take it as a warning for yourself, or do you assume it applies only to the 'worst' criminals? What does that reveal about your view of Allah's justice?
?
Razi insists that the general wording of the verse applies to everyone, including believers. Have you ever made excuses for your own sins by thinking Allah's mercy will exempt you from punishment? How does this principle challenge that assumption?
?
If you truly believed that every intentional evil deed will be requited (4:123), would you change one habit today? What holds you back from taking that verse literally?

Four Straightforward Verses Against the Murji'ah
Razi's third through sixth proofs, each a single verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see how Razi uses four clear Quranic verses (8:16, 99:7-8, 4:29-30, 20:74) to argue that punishment threatens all, not just disbelievers.

Core Idea
These verses speak of punishment without restricting to disbelievers.

Having established the principle of general wording, Razi now presents four straightforward verses that threaten severe punishment for specific sins. Each verse uses unconditional language, making them powerful evidence against the Murji'ah claim that only disbelievers face eternal torment.

Guided Path
1
Read the four proofs consecutively
Read proofs 3, 4, 5, and 6 in Arabic and translation. Notice how each verse describes punishment without mentioning belief or disbelief.
These are simple but cumulative.
2
Identify the common pattern
Each proof uses a conditional or general particle (man, ma) to encompass anyone who performs the act.
This reinforces the generality principle.
3
Reflect on the cumulative force
Ask: Why does Razi cite multiple verses? The repetition strengthens the case that threat includes believers.
Notice the variety of sins: desertion, evil deeds, injustice, criminality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِنَا مُّتَعَمِّدًا فَجَزَاؤُهُ جَهَنَّمُ خَالِدًا فِيهَا﴾ [النساء : ۹۳] وإذا ثبت أن جزاءه ذلك وجب أن يصل إليه، لقوله تعالى: ﴿مَن يَعْمَلْ سُوءًا يُجْزَ بِهِ﴾ [النساء : ۱۲۳] لا يقال : نزلت في بعض الكفار ؛ لأنا نقول : العبرة بعموم اللفظ لا بخصوص السبب. الحجة الثالثة : قوله تعالى: ﴿يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذا لَقِيتُمُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا زَحْفًا ... وَمَن يُوَلِّهِمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ دُبُرَهُ إِلَّا مُتَحَرِّفًا لِقِتَالٍ أَوْ مُتَحَيِّزًا إِلَى فِئَةٍ فَقَدْ بَاءَ بِغَضَبٍ مِنَ اللهِ وَمَأْوَاهُ جَهَنَّمُ وَبِئْسَ الْمَصِيرُ﴾ [الأنفال : ١٦] الحجة الرابعة : قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ خَيْرًا يَرَهُ وَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ شَرًّا يَرَهُ﴾ [الزلزلة : ۷ - ۸] . الحجة الخامسة: قوله تعالى: ﴿يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا تَأْكُلُوا أَمْوَالَكُمْ بَيْنَكُم بِالْبَاطِلِ﴾ [النساء : ۲۹] إلى قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يَفْعَلْ ذَلِكَ عُدْوَانًا وَظُلْمًا فَسَوْفَ نُصْلِيهِ نَارًا﴾ [النساء : ٣٠] . الحجة السادسة: قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّهُ مَن يَأْتِ رَبَّهُ مُجْرِمًا فَإِنَّ لَهُ جَهَنَّمَ لَا يَمُوتُ فِيهَا وَلَا يَحْيَا﴾ [طه: ٧٤]. الحجة السابعة : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَقَدْ خَابَ مَنْ حَمَلَ ظُلْمًا﴾ [طه: ۱۱۱] ولا شك أن هذا الوعيد يتناول الظالم سواء كان كافرًا أو مؤمنًا. الحجة الثامنة : أنه تعالى قال بعد تعديد المعاصي : ﴿وَمَن يَفْعَلْ ذَلِكَ يَلْقَ أَثَامًا يُضَاعَفْ لَهُ الْعَذَابُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ وَيَخْلُدْ فِيهِ مُهَانًا﴾ [الفرقان: ٦٨ - ٦٩] . الحجة التاسعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن جَاءَ بِالْحَسَنَةِ فَلَهُ خَيْرٌ مِنْهَا وَهُم مِّن فَزَعٍ يَوْمَئِذٍ آمِنُونَ وَمَن جَاءَ بِالسَّيِّئَةِ فَكُبَّتْ وُجُوهُهُمْ فِي النَّارِ هَلْ تُجْزَوْنَ إِلَّا مَا كُنتُمْ تَعْمَلُونَ﴾ [النمل: ۸۹ - ۹۰] فلما دل النصف الأول من هذه الآية على أن الوعد حاصل على الطاعات دل النصف الثاني على أن الوعيد حاصل على جميع المعاصي. الحجة العاشرة : قوله تعالى : ﴿فَأَمَّا مَن طَغَى وَآثَرَ الْحَيَاةَ الدُّنْيَا فَإِنَّ الْجَحِيمَ هِيَ الْمَأْوَى﴾ [النازعات : ٣٧ - ٣٩]. الحجة الحادية عشرة : أنه تعالى حكى قول المرجئة، فقال : ﴿وَقَالُوا لَن تَمَسَّنَا النَّارُ إِلَّا أَيَّامًا مَّعْدُودَةً﴾ [البَقَرَة : ۸۰] ثم إنه تعالى كذبهم في هذه المقالة بقوله : ﴿قُلْ أَخَذْتُمْ عِندَ اللهِ عَهْدًا فَلَنْ يُخْلِفَ اللهُ عَهْدَهُ أَمْ تَقُولُونَ عَلَى اللهِ مَا لَا تَعْلَمُونَ﴾ [البقرة : ٨٠] ثم ذكر المذهب الصحيح فقال : ﴿بَلَى مَن كَسَبَ سَيِّئَةً وَأَحَاطَتْ بِهِ خَطِيئَتُهُ فَأُولَئِكَ أَصْحَابُ النَّارِ هُمْ فِيهَا خَالِدُونَ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ۸۱].
The second proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding therein&quot; (Surah al-Nisa 4:93). And when it is established that his recompense is that, it must reach him, due to His saying, Exalted: &quot;Whoever does evil will be requited for it&quot; (Surah al-Nisa 4:123). It cannot be said: it was revealed concerning some disbelievers; because we say: consideration is given to the generality of the wording, not to the specificity of the cause. The third proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;O you who believe, when you meet those who disbelieve in battle... and whoever turns his back to them on that day, unless maneuvering for battle or joining a company, has indeed incurred the wrath of Allah, and his abode is Hell, and evil is the destination&quot; (Surah al-Anfal 8:16). The fourth proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;So whoever does an atom&#39;s weight of good will see it, and whoever does an atom&#39;s weight of evil will see it&quot; (Surah al-Zalzala 99:7-8). The fifth proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;O you who believe, do not consume your wealth among yourselves unjustly... and whoever does that in transgression and injustice, We will burn him in a fire&quot; (Surah al-Nisa 4:29-30). The sixth proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;Indeed, whoever comes to his Lord as a criminal, then for him is Hell; he will neither die therein nor live&quot; (Surah Ta-Ha 20:74). The seventh proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;And indeed he fails who carries injustice&quot; (Surah Ta-Ha 20:111). There is no doubt that this threat encompasses the oppressor, whether he is a disbeliever or a believer. The eighth proof: That He, Exalted, after enumerating sins, said: &quot;And whoever does that will meet a penalty; the punishment will be doubled for him on the Day of Resurrection, and he will abide therein humiliated&quot; (Surah al-Furqan 25:68-69). The ninth proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;And whoever comes with a good deed, for him is better than it, and they from the terror of that Day are secure. And whoever comes with an evil deed, their faces are thrust into the fire: &#39;Are you recompensed except for what you used to do?&#39;&quot; (Surah al-Naml 27:89-90). Since the first half of this verse indicates that the promise of reward is for acts of obedience, the second half indicates that the threat of punishment is for all acts of disobedience. The tenth proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;As for he who transgressed and preferred the life of this world, then indeed Hellfire is the refuge&quot; (Surah al-Nazi&#39;at 79:37-39). The eleventh proof: That He, Exalted, related the saying of the Murji&#39;ah: &quot;And they say, &#39;The fire will not touch us except for a limited number of days&#39;&quot; (Surah al-Baqara 2:80). Then He, Exalted, declared them false in this statement by His saying: &quot;Say, &#39;Have you taken a covenant with Allah? Then Allah will not break His covenant, or do you say about Allah what you do not know?&#39;&quot; (Surah al-Baqara 2:80). Then He mentioned the correct doctrine, saying: &quot;Yes, whoever earns evil and his sin surrounds him, those are the companions of the fire; they will abide therein eternally&quot; (Surah al-Baqara 2:81).
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage presents ten consecutive Quranic proofs (the second through the eleventh) supporting the position that divine threats of punishment encompass all sinners, including believers who commit major sins, contrary to the Murji&#39;ah view that only disbelievers are subject to eternal punishment. Each proof is a verse that imposes punishment in absolute or general terms. The second proof (4:93) threatens anyone who kills a believer intentionally with eternal Hell; Razi argues this applies even to a believer who kills another believer, and the principle of general wording (umum al-lafz) overrides any claim of specific cause. The third proof (8:16) threatens those who flee from battle with divine wrath and Hell. The fourth (99:7-8) promises reward and punishment for every atom&#39;s weight of good and evil, without restricting to disbelievers. The fifth (4:29-30) threatens fire for those who consume wealth unjustly. The sixth (20:74) states that every criminal who comes to his Lord will have Hell. The seventh (20:111) declares that anyone who bears injustice fails; Razi notes this includes both believer and disbeliever oppressors. The eighth (25:68-69) lists major sins and threatens doubled punishment and eternal abasement. The ninth (27:89-90) contrasts the security of those who bring good deeds with the casting into fire of those who bring evil deeds. The tenth (79:37-39) threatens Hell for those who transgress and prefer worldly life. The eleventh (2:80-81) directly refutes the Murji&#39;ah claim of limited punishment, asserting that those whose sin encompasses them are eternal inhabitants of the fire. Razi&#39;s method is to cite clear Quranic texts that either explicitly mention eternity for certain sins or use conditional particles like 'man' (whoever) and 'ma' (whatever) to indicate generality. The underlying principle is that these verses do not differentiate between believers and disbelievers in their threat, so they apply to all who commit the described sins.

Checkpoint
Which of the following threats is described as 'eternal' (khalid/la yamut) in the verses?
A) The threat in Surah al-Anfal 8:16
B) The threat in Surah al-Zalzala 99:7-8
C) The threat in Surah al-Nisa 4:29-30
D) The threat in Surah Ta-Ha 20:74

Key Takeaway
These four verses prove that punishment is tied to the sin itself, not to the status of the sinner as a disbeliever.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you assume Allah will overlook it because you are a believer? How does 99:7-8 challenge that assumption about 'atom's weight'?
?
Think of a specific sin you have committed. Do you truly believe you will see its consequence? What would change in your daily life if you took that verse literally?
?
The Murji'ah felt secure by saying sin doesn't affect faith. Are there areas in your life where you rely on your faith status rather than your actions? What step will you take today to align your practice with the warning of these verses?

Three Emphatic Proofs from Clear Threats
Razi's seventh, eighth, and ninth proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses three verses (20:111, 25:68-69, 27:89-90) to emphasize that divine threats encompass oppressors and evil-doers regardless of faith.

Core Idea
Injustice and evil deeds bring divine punishment whether one is a believer or not.

Razi now presents three more proofs that explicitly state punishment for specific sins or general evil. These verses reinforce the pattern: the threat is universal. The seventh proof even notes that the verse applies to both believing and disbelieving oppressors.

Guided Path
1
Read the three proofs (7-9)
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that the seventh proof includes an explicit statement that the threat includes both believers and disbelievers.
This is a key moment.
2
Analyze the ninth proof's structure
The ninth proof is a verse with two halves: promise for good, threat for evil. Razi explicitly notes the logical inference.
Understand the contrast.
3
Reflect on the cumulative evidence
Ask: How do these proofs strengthen the case? They cover different sins and use strong language like 'loss', 'doubled punishment', and 'thrust into fire'.
Notice the variety.

Commentary
This passage presents ten consecutive Quranic proofs (the second through the eleventh) supporting the position that divine threats of punishment encompass all sinners, including believers who commit major sins, contrary to the Murji&#39;ah view that only disbelievers are subject to eternal punishment. Each proof is a verse that imposes punishment in absolute or general terms. The second proof (4:93) threatens anyone who kills a believer intentionally with eternal Hell; Razi argues this applies even to a believer who kills another believer, and the principle of general wording (umum al-lafz) overrides any claim of specific cause. The third proof (8:16) threatens those who flee from battle with divine wrath and Hell. The fourth (99:7-8) promises reward and punishment for every atom&#39;s weight of good and evil, without restricting to disbelievers. The fifth (4:29-30) threatens fire for those who consume wealth unjustly. The sixth (20:74) states that every criminal who comes to his Lord will have Hell. The seventh (20:111) declares that anyone who bears injustice fails; Razi notes this includes both believer and disbeliever oppressors. The eighth (25:68-69) lists major sins and threatens doubled punishment and eternal abasement. The ninth (27:89-90) contrasts the security of those who bring good deeds with the casting into fire of those who bring evil deeds. The tenth (79:37-39) threatens Hell for those who transgress and prefer worldly life. The eleventh (2:80-81) directly refutes the Murji&#39;ah claim of limited punishment, asserting that those whose sin encompasses them are eternal inhabitants of the fire. Razi&#39;s method is to cite clear Quranic texts that either explicitly mention eternity for certain sins or use conditional particles like 'man' (whoever) and 'ma' (whatever) to indicate generality. The underlying principle is that these verses do not differentiate between believers and disbelievers in their threat, so they apply to all who commit the described sins.

Refuting the Murji'ah with the Eleventh Proof
Razi's eleventh proof refuting the Murji'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the Murji'ah's own claim and Allah's refutation in Surah al-Baqara 2:80-81 to prove that believers who are surrounded by sin will have eternal punishment.

Core Idea
Allah refutes the Murji'ah and declares eternal fire for those engulfed by sin.

The final proof is the most direct: Razi quotes the Murji'ah's statement that they will only be punished for a few days, then shows how Allah refutes them and establishes the correct doctrine—that those whose sins surround them will abide in the fire eternally. This is a powerful conclusion to the series.

Guided Path
1
Read the eleventh proof
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the structure: quote of Murji'ah, refutation, and then positive statement.
This is a three-part argument.
2
Identify the refutation
Find how Allah refutes the Murji'ah: by asking if they have a covenant or are speaking without knowledge.
Then the correct position follows.
3
Understand the condition of 'ihatah'
The verse says 'whoever earns evil and his sin surrounds him' will be eternal. This is the key condition.
This includes believers who persist in sin.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِنَا مُّتَعَمِّدًا فَجَزَاؤُهُ جَهَنَّمُ خَالِدًا فِيهَا﴾ [النساء : ۹۳] وإذا ثبت أن جزاءه ذلك وجب أن يصل إليه، لقوله تعالى: ﴿مَن يَعْمَلْ سُوءًا يُجْزَ بِهِ﴾ [النساء : ۱۲۳] لا يقال : نزلت في بعض الكفار ؛ لأنا نقول : العبرة بعموم اللفظ لا بخصوص السبب. الحجة الثالثة : قوله تعالى: ﴿يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذا لَقِيتُمُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا زَحْفًا ... وَمَن يُوَلِّهِمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ دُبُرَهُ إِلَّا مُتَحَرِّفًا لِقِتَالٍ أَوْ مُتَحَيِّزًا إِلَى فِئَةٍ فَقَدْ بَاءَ بِغَضَبٍ مِنَ اللهِ وَمَأْوَاهُ جَهَنَّمُ وَبِئْسَ الْمَصِيرُ﴾ [الأنفال : ١٦] الحجة الرابعة : قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ خَيْرًا يَرَهُ وَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ شَرًّا يَرَهُ﴾ [الزلزلة : ۷ - ۸] . الحجة الخامسة: قوله تعالى: ﴿يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا تَأْكُلُوا أَمْوَالَكُمْ بَيْنَكُم بِالْبَاطِلِ﴾ [النساء : ۲۹] إلى قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يَفْعَلْ ذَلِكَ عُدْوَانًا وَظُلْمًا فَسَوْفَ نُصْلِيهِ نَارًا﴾ [النساء : ٣٠] . الحجة السادسة: قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّهُ مَن يَأْتِ رَبَّهُ مُجْرِمًا فَإِنَّ لَهُ جَهَنَّمَ لَا يَمُوتُ فِيهَا وَلَا يَحْيَا﴾ [طه: ٧٤]. الحجة السابعة : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَقَدْ خَابَ مَنْ حَمَلَ ظُلْمًا﴾ [طه: ۱۱۱] ولا شك أن هذا الوعيد يتناول الظالم سواء كان كافرًا أو مؤمنًا. الحجة الثامنة : أنه تعالى قال بعد تعديد المعاصي : ﴿وَمَن يَفْعَلْ ذَلِكَ يَلْقَ أَثَامًا يُضَاعَفْ لَهُ الْعَذَابُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ وَيَخْلُدْ فِيهِ مُهَانًا﴾ [الفرقان: ٦٨ - ٦٩] . الحجة التاسعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن جَاءَ بِالْحَسَنَةِ فَلَهُ خَيْرٌ مِنْهَا وَهُم مِّن فَزَعٍ يَوْمَئِذٍ آمِنُونَ وَمَن جَاءَ بِالسَّيِّئَةِ فَكُبَّتْ وُجُوهُهُمْ فِي النَّارِ هَلْ تُجْزَوْنَ إِلَّا مَا كُنتُمْ تَعْمَلُونَ﴾ [النمل: ۸۹ - ۹۰] فلما دل النصف الأول من هذه الآية على أن الوعد حاصل على الطاعات دل النصف الثاني على أن الوعيد حاصل على جميع المعاصي. الحجة العاشرة : قوله تعالى : ﴿فَأَمَّا مَن طَغَى وَآثَرَ الْحَيَاةَ الدُّنْيَا فَإِنَّ الْجَحِيمَ هِيَ الْمَأْوَى﴾ [النازعات : ٣٧ - ٣٩]. الحجة الحادية عشرة : أنه تعالى حكى قول المرجئة، فقال : ﴿وَقَالُوا لَن تَمَسَّنَا النَّارُ إِلَّا أَيَّامًا مَّعْدُودَةً﴾ [البَقَرَة : ۸۰] ثم إنه تعالى كذبهم في هذه المقالة بقوله : ﴿قُلْ أَخَذْتُمْ عِندَ اللهِ عَهْدًا فَلَنْ يُخْلِفَ اللهُ عَهْدَهُ أَمْ تَقُولُونَ عَلَى اللهِ مَا لَا تَعْلَمُونَ﴾ [البقرة : ٨٠] ثم ذكر المذهب الصحيح فقال : ﴿بَلَى مَن كَسَبَ سَيِّئَةً وَأَحَاطَتْ بِهِ خَطِيئَتُهُ فَأُولَئِكَ أَصْحَابُ النَّارِ هُمْ فِيهَا خَالِدُونَ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ۸۱].
The second proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding therein&quot; (Surah al-Nisa 4:93). And when it is established that his recompense is that, it must reach him, due to His saying, Exalted: &quot;Whoever does evil will be requited for it&quot; (Surah al-Nisa 4:123). It cannot be said: it was revealed concerning some disbelievers; because we say: consideration is given to the generality of the wording, not to the specificity of the cause. The third proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;O you who believe, when you meet those who disbelieve in battle... and whoever turns his back to them on that day, unless maneuvering for battle or joining a company, has indeed incurred the wrath of Allah, and his abode is Hell, and evil is the destination&quot; (Surah al-Anfal 8:16). The fourth proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;So whoever does an atom&#39;s weight of good will see it, and whoever does an atom&#39;s weight of evil will see it&quot; (Surah al-Zalzala 99:7-8). The fifth proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;O you who believe, do not consume your wealth among yourselves unjustly... and whoever does that in transgression and injustice, We will burn him in a fire&quot; (Surah al-Nisa 4:29-30). The sixth proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;Indeed, whoever comes to his Lord as a criminal, then for him is Hell; he will neither die therein nor live&quot; (Surah Ta-Ha 20:74). The seventh proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;And indeed he fails who carries injustice&quot; (Surah Ta-Ha 20:111). There is no doubt that this threat encompasses the oppressor, whether he is a disbeliever or a believer. The eighth proof: That He, Exalted, after enumerating sins, said: &quot;And whoever does that will meet a penalty; the punishment will be doubled for him on the Day of Resurrection, and he will abide therein humiliated&quot; (Surah al-Furqan 25:68-69). The ninth proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;And whoever comes with a good deed, for him is better than it, and they from the terror of that Day are secure. And whoever comes with an evil deed, their faces are thrust into the fire: &#39;Are you recompensed except for what you used to do?&#39;&quot; (Surah al-Naml 27:89-90). Since the first half of this verse indicates that the promise of reward is for acts of obedience, the second half indicates that the threat of punishment is for all acts of disobedience. The tenth proof: His saying, Exalted: &quot;As for he who transgressed and preferred the life of this world, then indeed Hellfire is the refuge&quot; (Surah al-Nazi&#39;at 79:37-39). The eleventh proof: That He, Exalted, related the saying of the Murji&#39;ah: &quot;And they say, &#39;The fire will not touch us except for a limited number of days&#39;&quot; (Surah al-Baqara 2:80). Then He, Exalted, declared them false in this statement by His saying: &quot;Say, &#39;Have you taken a covenant with Allah? Then Allah will not break His covenant, or do you say about Allah what you do not know?&#39;&quot; (Surah al-Baqara 2:80). Then He mentioned the correct doctrine, saying: &quot;Yes, whoever earns evil and his sin surrounds him, those are the companions of the fire; they will abide therein eternally&quot; (Surah al-Baqara 2:81).

Al-Razi's Four Responses to the Mu'tazilite Tarjih
Al-Razi responds with four counter-arguments to the first Mu'tazilite tarjih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's four counter-arguments that neutralize the Mu'tazilite proof for prioritizing warnings over promises.

Core Idea
Symmetry, contradiction, conditionality, and linguistic precision refute the Mu'tazilite tarjih.

The Mu'tazilites argued that worldly punishments (like curses and ḥadd) indicate afterlife punishment, thus verses of threat outweigh those of promise. Al-Razi, representing the Ashʿarī position, responds with four sharp counter-arguments. This passage shows how he systematically dismantles their reasoning using symmetrical reasoning, logical contradiction, analogical conditioning, and a linguistic point about the term 'jazā''. Let's follow his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazilite position
Recall that the Mu'tazilites gave preponderance (tarjīḥ) to verses of threat using worldly punishments as evidence. This is the claim al-Razi is refuting.
The first tarjīḥ is based on verses mentioning curses and punishments in this world.
2
Read al-Razi's first counter-argument
Notice how he points out symmetry: just as worldly punishments exist, worldly honors also exist for believers. So either both sides are balanced or neither is stronger.
He uses Quran 6:54 as an example of worldly honor.
3
Examine the second and third arguments
The second argument says that promise verses contradict any verse implying afterlife threat, so the Mu'tazilite evidence is neutralized. The third draws an analogy from the thief verse: worldly punishment is conditioned on no repentance, so afterlife punishment may be conditioned on no pardon.
4
Study the fourth linguistic argument
Al-Razi argues that 'jazā'' means 'what suffices', so the ḥadd being called a jazā' implies it is sufficient punishment, precluding afterlife punishment.
This turns the Mu'tazilite proof against itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أجاب أصحابنا عن الترجيح الأول من وجوه:
الأول: أنه لما وجدت آيات دالة على أنهم يلعنون ويذمون ويعذبون في الدنيا بسبب معاصيهم كذلك أيضا حصلت آيات دالة على أنهم يعظمون ويمدحون الدنيا بسبب إيمانهم قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا جَاءَكَ الَّذِينَ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِآيَاتِنَا فَقُلْ سَلامُ عَلَيْكُمْ كَتَبَ رَبُّكُمْ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ الرَّحْمَةَ﴾ [الأنعام: ٥٤] فهم يرجحون الآيات الدالة على حصول الوعيد في الآخرة بالآيات الدالة على حصول اللعن والذم في الدنيا، ونحن أيضًا نرجح الآيات الدالة على حصول وعد الإحسان والعفو في الآخرة بالآيات الدالة على حصول المدح والتعظيم في الدنيا، فلم كان قولهم أرجح من قولنا؟ بل كان الترجيح معًا من الوجوه المذكورة. أقصى ما في الباب أن يقال: فإن كان لا يلعن ولا يذم في الدنيا فلم يقام في الدنيا عليه الحد؟
فتقول: هذا ضعيف؛ لأن الحد قد يقام على سبيل التنكيل، ألا ترى أن التائب قد يقام عليه الحد وليس هناك لعن ولا نكال فعلمنا أنه لا يمكن الاستدلال بإقامة الحد على حصول استحقاق العذاب.
الوجه الثاني: أن آيات الوعد كما أنها معارضة لآيات الوعيد، فكذلك هي معارضة لكل آية دالة على معنى يستلزم حصول الوعيد في الآخرة، وعندكم أن الآيات الدالة على حصول اللعن والخزي والنكال والعذاب في الدنيا مستلزمة لحصول الوعيد في الآخرة، فيحصل التعارض بين هذه الآيات وبين آيات الوعيد، وإذا حصل التعارض في هذا المقام لم تكن هذه الآيات مرجحة لآيات الوعد على آيات الوعيد، فيبقى ما ذكرناه من الترجيحات سليمًا عن المعارض.
الثالث: أن قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالسَّارِقُ وَالسَّارِقَةُ﴾ [المائدة: ٣٨] شرع القطع في حقهما فهو جزاء بما كسبا نَكَالاً مِّنَ اللهِ ﴾ [المائدة: ٣٨] وأجمعنا على أن حصول هذا المعنى مشروط بعدم التوبة، فكذلك ههنا أيضًا لم لا يجوز أن يكون حصول هذا المعنى مشروطًا بعدم العفو؟
الرابع: أن هذه الآيات حجة عليكم من وجوه أخر؛ وذلك لأن الجزاء اسم لما يكفي، وإذا حكم الله بأن الحد الذي يقام عليه في الدنيا جزاء، وثبت أن الجزاء ما كان كافيًا، كان ظاهر هذه الآية مانعًا من إيصال العقاب إليه في الآخرة، فثبت أن الترجيح الذي ذكرتموه يبطل مذهبكم بالكلية.
Our companions answered the first tarjīḥ (preference) from several aspects:
First: Just as there are verses indicating that they are cursed, blamed, and punished in this world due to their sins, so too there have come verses indicating that they are honored and praised in this world due to their faith. Allah said: {And when those who believe in Our verses come to you, say, 'Peace be upon you. Your Lord has prescribed mercy upon Himself'} [al-Anʿām 6:54]. They give preponderance to the verses indicating the occurrence of threat in the afterlife by the verses indicating the occurrence of cursing and blame in this world, and we also give preponderance to the verses indicating the occurrence of the promise of beneficence and pardon in the afterlife by the verses indicating the occurrence of praise and honor in this world. So why is their statement more preponderant than ours? Rather, both preponderances are equal from the mentioned aspects. The most that can be said is: 'If he is not cursed or blamed in this world, why is the ḥadd (prescribed punishment) established against him in this world?'
To this we say: This is weak, because the ḥadd may be established by way of exemplary punishment. Do you not see that the penitent person may have the ḥadd established against him even though there is no curse or punishment? So we know that it is not possible to infer from the establishment of the ḥadd the obtaining of the desert of punishment.
Second: Just as the verses of promise contradict the verses of threat, so too they contradict every verse indicating a meaning that entails the occurrence of threat in the afterlife. According to you, the verses indicating the occurrence of cursing, humiliation, punishment, and torment in this world entail the occurrence of threat in the afterlife. Thus there is contradiction between these verses and the verses of threat. When contradiction occurs in this context, these verses do not give preponderance to the verses of promise over the verses of threat, and thus what we have mentioned of preponderances remains free of contradiction.
Third: Allah's statement {And the thief, male and female} [al-Māʾida 5:38] legislates amputation regarding them, so it is a requital for what they earned, a deterrent punishment from Allah. We all agree that this meaning is conditioned upon the absence of repentance. So likewise here, why is it not permissible that this meaning be conditioned upon the absence of pardon?
Fourth: These verses are an argument against you from other aspects; this is because 'al-jazā'' (requital) is a term for what suffices. When Allah rules that the ḥadd established in this world is a requital, and it is established that the requital is what suffices, then the apparent meaning of this verse prevents the delivery of punishment to him in the afterlife. Thus it is established that the tarjīḥ you mentioned refutes your doctrine entirely.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the first Mu'tazilite argument for prioritizing the verses of threat (waʿīd) over the verses of promise (waʿd). Al-Razi presents four counter-arguments following his companions' response. First, he points out symmetry: just as the Mu'tazilites use worldly punishments to support afterlife threat, Muslims can use worldly honors (like praise in the Quran) to support afterlife reward; thus no side is stronger. He then dismisses the objection about ḥadd punishments by noting that even a penitent person can be punished in this world without implying afterlife punishment. Second, he argues that the verses of promise contradict not only the threat verses but also any verse implying afterlife threat, so the Mu'tazilite reliance on worldly punishment verses is neutralized. Third, he draws an analogy from the thief verse: the worldly punishment is conditioned on lack of repentance, so similarly, afterlife punishment may be conditioned on lack of pardon. Fourth, he uses the linguistic point that 'jazā'' means 'what suffices', so the worldly punishment being called 'jazā'' implies it is sufficient, thereby precluding further punishment in the afterlife. Thus the Mu'tazilite tarjīḥ actually refutes their own position.

Key Terms
ترجيح
وعيد
وعد
حد
جزاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believing that the Mu'tazilite use of worldly punishment verses is a decisive proof for prioritizing threat verses.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that such verses are either symmetrical (and thus neutral), contradicted by promise verses, conditioned on repentance/pardon, or sufficient in themselves (jazā') so they preclude afterlife punishment.

Checkpoint
According to al-Razi's fourth counter-argument, why does calling the ḥadd a 'jazā'' refute the Mu'tazilite position?
A) Because 'jazā'' means 'punishment' and thus confirms afterlife punishment.
B) Because 'jazā'' means 'what suffices', so the worldly punishment is sufficient.
C) Because 'jazā'' implies gratitude, so no punishment is due.
D) Because 'jazā'' is specific to thieves and cannot be generalized.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's four counter-arguments demonstrate that the Mu'tazilite tarjīḥ based on worldly punishments is inconclusive and can be turned against them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face hardship or punishment in this world, do you immediately assume it means God is angry and has abandoned you? How does al-Razi's argument that worldly punishment can be a deterrent rather than a sign of afterlife doom change how you interpret your trials? Will you now pause to consider that God's mercy may override any worldly consequence?
?
Are you quicker to believe that God will punish you for your sins than that He will forgive you? Al-Razi shows that verses of promise can outweigh verses of threat through proper reasoning. Do you truly allow the promise of God's mercy to outweigh your fear of punishment in your daily life, or do you live in constant anxiety? Commit to reciting a verse of promise daily for a week and reflect on its impact on your hope.
?
Do you judge others based on their worldly circumstances—assuming those who suffer are being punished and those who prosper are favored? Al-Razi's symmetry argument exposes the fallacy of such judgments. Will you now refrain from assuming God's final verdict based on outward conditions, and instead treat every person's ultimate fate as known only to Him?

Reversing the Generality Argument on Promise and Threat Verses
Al-Razi denies that promise verses are more general than threat verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi overturns the Mu'tazilite claim that promise verses are general by demonstrating that threat verses are actually more comprehensive in scope.

Core Idea
Threat verses are more general than promise verses.

The Mu'tazilites argued that verses of promise (waʿd) are general and thus weigh in their favor. Al-Razi responds directly by denying this premise. He shows that, far from being general, promise/pardon verses are restricted to believers, while threat verses cover everyone—believers and disbelievers alike, before and after repentance. This short but powerful rebuttal flips the argument on its head.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation to get a feel for al-Razi's concise argument.
Notice the phrase 'هذا ممنوع' which is a direct denial.
2
Identify the two parts of the rebuttal
Al-Razi first denies the claim, then provides a reasoning clause starting with 'وذلك لأن'. Identify the specific points he makes about threat verses and pardon verses.
He gives two scoops: threat verses include all, pardon verses are specific.
3
Analyze the logical reversal
The Mu'tazilites claimed promise verses are general and threat verses are specific. Al-Razi argues the opposite. Ask yourself: what does this reversal imply for the overall debate?
This shows that textual evidence can be reinterpreted to support the orthodox position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الترجيح الثاني: - وهو أن آيات الوعد عامة - فنقول: هذا ممنوع، وذلك لأن آيات الوعيد يدخل فيها الكافر والمؤمن من قبل التوبة ومن بعدها، وآيات العفو مختصة بالمؤمن، فثبت أن الآيات التي تمسكنا بها خاصة والآيات التي تمسكتم بها عامة.
As for the second tarjīḥ—that the verses of promise are general—we say: this is denied. This is because the verses of threat include the disbeliever and the believer before repentance and after it, while the verses of pardon are specific to the believer. Thus it is established that the verses we hold are specific and the verses you hold are general.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage is a rebuttal of the second Mu'tazilite argument, which claimed that verses of promise (waʿd) are general while verses of threat (waʿīd) are specific. Al-Razi denies this and argues the opposite: verses of threat are actually more general because they encompass both the believer and the disbeliever, whether before or after repentance. In contrast, verses of pardon (ʿafw) are restricted to believers. Therefore, the verses that the orthodox party (the author's school) rely on are specific (i.e., pardon verses), while the verses the Mu'tazilites rely on (threat verses) are general. This reverses the claimed priority, undermining the Mu'tazilite tarjīḥ.

Key Terms
ترجيح
عام
خاص
وعيد
وعد
عفو

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that verses of promise (like those about mercy) are broader in scope than verses of threat.
Correction: Al-Razi shows the opposite: threat verses cover both believers and disbelievers, before and after repentance, while promise/pardon verses are limited to believers. Therefore, threat verses are more general.

Checkpoint
According to al-Razi, why are the verses of threat more general than the verses of pardon?
A) Because they refer only to disbelievers.
B) Because they include both believers and disbelievers before and after repentance.
C) Because they are found in more chapters of the Quran.
D) Because they are unconditional.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi overturns the Mu'tazilite tarjīḥ by demonstrating that threat verses are general and pardon verses are specific, not the other way around.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Razi's Three Arguments Against Mu'tazilite Objections on Punishment
Razi refutes Mu'tazilite objections with three arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi refutes Mu'tazilite objections to divine punishment using three distinct arguments.

Core Idea
Razi uses language, scope, and priority to defend divine mercy over punishment.

In this passage, Imam Razi presents a multi-pronged refutation of Mu'tazilite claims about divine punishment. He tackles their arguments from the meaning of 'recompense', the generality of verses, and the hierarchy of divine attributes. This lesson will walk through each of his arguments and how they systematically undermine the Mu'tazilite position.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic text and its literal translation to grasp the overall flow of arguments.
Notice the structure: Razi presents three distinct points.
2
Analyze the first argument (sufficiency of punishment)
Focus on Razi's claim that 'al-jaza' means what suffices. Understand how this undermines the need for further punishment in the afterlife.
This argument is based on the meaning of the word 'jaza'.
3
Analyze the second argument (generality vs specificity of verses)
Examine Razi's rebuttal that verses of threat apply generally, while verses of pardon are specific to believers. This denies the Mu'tazilite claim that their verses are general.
Note the distinction between 'Ayat al-Wa'id' and 'Ayat al-Afwa'.
4
Analyze the third argument (essential vs incidental purposes)
Understand Razi's point that mercy is intended essentially, punishment incidentally, so priority should be given to mercy.
This is a logical and theological argument.
5
Reflect on the overall refutation
Consider how each argument addresses different aspects of the Mu'tazilite objection and how they collectively dismantle it.
Razi concludes the discussion with 'This completes the discussion...'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع : أن هذه الآيات حجة عليكم من وجوه أخر ؛ وذلك لأن الجزاء اسم لما يكفي، وإذا حكم الله بأن الحد الذي يقام عليه في الدنيا جزاء، وثبت أن الجزاء ما كان كافيًا، كان ظاهر هذه الآية مانعا من إيصال العقاب إليه في الآخرة، فثبت أن الترجيح الذي ذكرتموه يبطل مذهبكم بالكلية.
وأما الترجيح الثاني: - وهو أن آيات الوعد عامة - فنقول: هذا ممنوع، وذلك لأن آيات الوعيد يدخل فيها الكافر والمؤمن من قبل التوبة ومن بعدها، وآيان العفو مختصة بالمؤمن، فثبت أن الآيات التي تمسكنا بها خاصة والآيات التي تمسكتم بها عامة.
وأما الترجيح الثالث : فضعيف لأن الرحمة مقصودة بالذات، والتعذيب مقصود بالعرض، وترجيح ما هو مقصود بالذات على ما هو مقصود بالتبع والعرض أولى من العكس.
هذا تمام الكلام في الجواب عن شبهات المعتزلة، وبالله التوفيق.
The fourth: that these verses are an argument against you from other aspects; because 'al-jaza' (recompense) is a name for what suffices. And when God has judged that the legal punishment (al-hadd) imposed in this world is a recompense, and it is established that the recompense is what suffices, then the apparent meaning of this verse prevents the infliction of punishment upon him in the Hereafter. So it is established that the weighting (al-tarjih) you mentioned nullifies your doctrine entirely.
As for the second weighting: that the verses of promise are general. We say: this is denied, because the verses of threat include both the disbeliever and the believer before repentance and after it, while the verses of pardon are specific to the believer. So it is established that the verses we hold to are specific, and the verses you hold to are general.
As for the third weighting: it is weak, because mercy is intended essentially, while punishment is intended incidentally, and giving priority to what is intended essentially over what is intended as subsidiary and incidental is better than the opposite.
This completes the discussion on answering the doubts of the Mu'tazilites, and with God is success.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Mu'tazilite objections. Razi presents three arguments (a fourth point and two additional weightings) to undermine the Mu'tazilite position. He first argues that the verse about the punishment of thieves states that the prescribed punishment in this world is a sufficient recompense, so no further punishment is needed in the afterlife. Second, he argues that verses of threat apply generally to believers and disbelievers, while verses of pardon are specific to believers, so the Mu'tazilites cannot claim their verses are general. Third, he argues that mercy is primary, punishment secondary, so priority should be given to mercy over punishment. He concludes the refutation.

Key Terms
الجزاء
الحد
الترجيح
آيات الوعيد
آيات العفو

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilite objections to divine punishment are not answered by Ash'ari scholars.
Correction: Imam Razi provides a systematic refutation using linguistic, scriptural, and logical arguments.

Checkpoint
Why does Razi consider the Mu'tazilite second weighting (that verses of promise are general) invalid?
A) Verses of promise are not general because they only apply to the afterlife.
B) Verses of threat include both believer and disbeliever, while verses of pardon are specific to believers.
C) Verses of promise are abrogated by verses of threat.
D) The Mu'tazilites do not accept the authority of verses of promise.

Key Takeaway
Razi's refutation shows that Mu'tazilite objections are weak because they ignore the linguistic meaning of recompense, the specific scope of pardoning verses, and the priority of mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Razi argues that mercy is essential and punishment incidental. In your daily life, do you treat God's mercy as the foundation of your relationship with Him, or as an afterthought? What would change if you lived as though mercy is His primary intent for you?

If you were to fully internalize that God's pardon is specifically for believers and that His threat includes all, would you live more boldly in hope or more cautiously in fear? What concrete step can you take this week to anchor your heart in His mercy rather than your own merits?

Temporary Punishment of Sinful Believers
Razi states Ash'ari position and gives a two-premise proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position on temporary punishment of sinful believers and the rational proof that supports it.

Core Idea
Sinful believers are punished temporarily, not eternally.

Imam Razi addresses a key theological dispute between the Ash'aris and the Mu'tazila: the fate of believers who commit major sins. While the Mu'tazila argue for eternal punishment, the Ash'aris affirm that such punishment is temporary and ultimately leads to Paradise. Razi provides a rational proof based on the coexistence of merit for reward and demerit for punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to grasp the main claims and flow of argument.
2
Identify the two positions
Notice the clear contrast: Ash'ari (temporary punishment) vs. Mu'tazila (eternal punishment). Understand what is at stake.
3
Follow the two-premise proof
Razi's proof has two premises. Break them down: the first premise about prior reward, the second about whether sin incurs punishment and its effect on prior reward.
The proof uses a logical disjunction: either the sinner deserves punishment or not.
4
Reflect on the concept of balancing
Consider the idea of muwazana (balancing) that Razi introduces as a possible objection. It sets up the next part of the discussion.
This prepares for the refutation of the Mu'tazila balancing argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة السادسة والثلاثون في أن وعيد الفساق منقطع مذهبنا : أنه تعالى وإن عذب الفساق من أهل الصلاة إلا أنه لا يتركهم في النار دائما، بل يخرجهم إلى الجنة. وقالت المعتزلة : إن الفاسق يبقى في النار دائما. والمعتمد لنا في هذه المسألة: أن هذا الفاسق إما أن لا يكون مستحقا للعقاب أو يكون مستحقا للعقاب لكنه ذلك أيضًا مستحق للثواب ومتى كان الأمر كذلك مع وجب أن يكون العقاب منقطعا. بيان المقدمة الأولى : أن هذا الفاسق قبل أن صدر عنه هذا الفسق كان الثواب بحكم إيمانه وسائر طاعاته، أما عندنا فبحكم الوعد، وأما عند الخصم فبحكم الاستحقاق، وإذا صدر عنه الفسق بعد ذلك فإما أن يصير بسبب ذلك الفسق مستحقا للعقاب أو لا يصير كذلك، فإن لم يصر مستحقا للعقاب فنقول : كان هذا الإنسان على هذا التقدير مستحقا للثواب، ولم يصر بسبب هذا الفعل مستحقا للعقاب، فوجب أن لا يعاقب فضلا عن أن يكون عقابه دائما . وأما إن قلنا : إنه صار بفسقه مستحقا للعقاب فنقول : استحقاق العقاب لا يزيل ما كان ثابتا له من استحقاق الثواب، وإذا كان كذلك وجب أن لا يكون عذابه دائما. وإنما قلنا : إن العقاب الطارئ لا يزيل الثواب المتقدم لأنه لو أزاله لكان إما أن يقال : الموازنة معتبرة أو غير معتبرة
The thirty-sixth question: on the threat to the sinners being interrupted. Our doctrine: that God Almighty, even if He punishes the sinners among the people of prayer, does not leave them in the Fire forever, but brings them out to Paradise. The Mu'tazila said: the sinner remains in the Fire forever. The relied-upon proof for us in this question is: that this sinner either does not deserve punishment or deserves punishment but also deserves reward, and when the matter is thus, then it is necessary that the punishment be interrupted. Explanation of the first premise: that this sinner, before committing this sin, had reward by virtue of his faith and other acts of obedience – according to us by virtue of the promise, and according to the opponent by virtue of entitlement. When he commits the sin thereafter, either he becomes deserving of punishment because of that sin or he does not. If he does not become deserving of punishment, we say: this person on this estimation is deserving of reward and did not become deserving of punishment because of this act, so he must not be punished, let alone that his punishment be eternal. And if we say that he became deserving of punishment by his sin, we say: the deserving of punishment does not remove what was established for him of deserving of reward. And if it is so, then his punishment must not be eternal. And we only say that the temporary punishment does not remove the prior reward because if it removed it, then it would be said either: muwazana (balancing) is considered or not considered.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage defines the issue and presents the Ash'ari position compared to the Mu'tazila. Razi begins by stating the Ash'ari doctrine: sinful believers will not remain in Hell forever but will eventually be brought to Paradise. He contrasts this with the Mu'tazilite view that such sinners remain eternally. He then gives the relied-upon proof, which rests on two premises. The first premise explains that before committing a major sin, the believer had reward due to faith and good deeds. The second premise considers two possibilities: either the sin makes the person deserving of punishment or not. If it does not, then clearly no eternal punishment. If it does, the deserving of punishment does not cancel the prior deserving of reward. Therefore the punishment cannot be eternal. He then introduces the concept of muwazana (balancing) as a possible objection: perhaps the temporary punishment could nullify the prior reward through balancing. This sets up the subsequent refutation.

Key Terms
الفساق
وعيد
منقطع
المعتزلة
استحقاق الثواب
استحقاق العقاب
الموازنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ash'ari position denies any punishment for sinful believers.
Correction: The Ash'ari position does not deny punishment; it only denies eternal punishment. Razi affirms that God may punish sinners temporarily before admitting them to Paradise.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari position presented by Razi, what is the fate of a sinful believer?

B) He will be punished temporarily then enter Paradise
C) He will not be punished at all
D) He will be annihilated

Key Takeaway
Sinful believers deserve temporary punishment, not eternal, because their prior reward for faith and obedience remains intact.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you truly believed that your prior good deeds remain even after sin, how would that change your daily struggle between obedience and falling into sin?
?
